## Error Diagnosis

The error is clear:

```
Cannot find patchField entry for topWall
```

The `0/T` file defines boundary patches: `upperWall`, `lowerWall`, `leftWall`, `rightWall`, and `frontAndBack`. However, the `blockMeshDict` defines boundary patches: `topWall`, `bottomWall`, `leftWall`, `rightWall`, `frontWall`, and `backWall`.

The mismatch is:
- `blockMeshDict` has `topWall` and `bottomWall`
- `0/T` has `upperWall` and `lowerWall`

## Proposed Solution

**Update the `0/T` file** to use the patch names that match `blockMeshDict`:

1. **Rename `upperWall` → `topWall`** and **`lowerWall` → `bottomWall`** in the `0/T` file's `boundaryField` section.
2. Keep all other boundary conditions (`leftWall`, `rightWall`, `frontAndBack`) as they are, since those names match between the files.

The `0/T` file should have:

```
boundaryField
{
    topWall
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform 305;
    }

    bottomWall
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform 300;
    }

    leftWall
    {
        type            zeroGradient;
    }

    rightWall
    {
        type            zeroGradient;
    }

    frontAndBack
    {
        type            empty;
    }
}
```

## Additional Notes

- **Consistency across all 0/ files**: Apply the same patch name corrections to all other field files in the `0/` directory:
  - `0/U`: `upperWall` → `topWall`, `lowerWall` → `bottomWall`
  - `0/alphat`: `upperWall` → `topWall`, `lowerWall` → `bottomWall`
  - `0/epsilon`: `upperWall` → `topWall`, `lowerWall` → `bottomWall`
  - `0/k`: `upperWall` → `topWall`, `lowerWall` → `bottomWall`
  - `0/nut`: `upperWall` → `topWall`, `lowerWall` → `bottomWall`
  - `0/p`: `upperWall` → `topWall`, `lowerWall` → `bottomWall`
  - `0/p_rgh`: `upperWall` → `topWall`, `lowerWall` → `bottomWall`

- **The `frontAndBack` patch name is correct** and should remain as-is since it matches the `blockMeshDict`.

This is a straightforward patch name mismatch that causes the solver to fail when trying to read boundary conditions. All other files appear correctly configured.

The error is:

```
Cannot find patchField entry for frontWall
```

- `topWall`

- `topWall`
- `bottomWall`
- `leftWall`
- `rightWall`
- `frontWall`
- `backWall`

The issue is that `0/T` has `frontAndBack` while `blockMeshDict` has `frontWall` and `backWall` as separate patches. The `frontAndBack` entry in `0/T` is a combined patch that doesn't exist in the mesh.

## Proposed Solution

**Update the `0/T` file** to match the exact patch names from `blockMeshDict`:

1. **Replace `frontAndBack` with separate entries for `frontWall` and `backWall`**:
   - `frontWall`: `type empty;`
   - `backWall`: `type empty;`

2. **Remove the `frontAndBack` entry entirely** from the `boundaryField` section.

============================== Reviewer Analysis ==============================
*** service=review, model_version=error_analysis ***
## Error Diagnosis

The error is:

```
patch type 'wall' not constraint type 'empty'
for patch frontWall of field T
```

This means the `frontWall` patch in the `0/T` file has `type empty;` but the solver expects a `wall` type constraint for this patch. Looking at the `blockMeshDict`, `frontWall` is indeed a `wall` type patch (not `empty`). The `empty` type is only appropriate for patches that are truly empty (like `frontAndBack` in the previous attempt, which was a combined patch).

## Proposed Solution

**Update the `0/T` file** — the `frontWall` and `backWall` boundary conditions should be `wall` type, not `empty`. The `empty` type is only used for patches that are actually empty (like the combined `frontAndBack` from the previous attempt). Since `frontWall` and `backWall` are real physical walls in the mesh, they should use `wall` boundary conditions.

The `0/T` file's `boundaryField` should be:

```
boundaryField
{
    topWall
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform 305;
    }

    bottomWall
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform 300;
    }

    leftWall
    {
        type            zeroGradient;
    }

    rightWall
    {
        type            zeroGradient;
    }

    frontWall
    {
        type            wall;
    }

    backWall
    {
        type            wall;
    }
}
```

## Additional Notes

- **Consistency across all 0/ files**: Apply the same patch type corrections to all other field files in the `0/` directory:
  - `0/U`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type noSlip;` (not `empty`)
  - `0/alphat`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type compressible::alphatWallFunction;` (not `empty`)
  - `0/epsilon`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type epsilonWallFunction;` (not `empty`)
  - `0/k`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type kqRWallFunction;` (not `empty`)
  - `0/nut`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type nutkWallFunction;` (not `empty`)
  - `0/p`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type calculated;` (not `empty`)
  - `0/p_rgh`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type fixedFluxPressure;` (not `empty`)

- **The `empty` type is only appropriate for patches that are truly empty** (like the combined `frontAndBack` patch from the previous attempt). Since `frontWall` and `backWall` are separate physical wall patches in the mesh, they should use the appropriate wall-type boundary conditions.

*** service=review, model_version=error_analysis ***
## Error Diagnosis

The error is:

```
Unknown patchField type wall for patch type wall
```

This means the solver is looking for a patch field type called `wall` but cannot find it in the list of valid types. Looking at the error message, the valid types include `compressible::alphatWallFunction`, `compressible::epsilonWallFunction`, `kqRWallFunction`, `nutkWallFunction`, etc., but **not** a generic `wall` type.

The issue is that the `0/T` file uses `type wall;` for the `frontWall` and `backWall` patches, but the solver expects a compressible-specific wall function type for these patches (since this is a compressible flow solver `buoyantFoam`). The `wall` type is not a valid patch field type for `buoyantFoam` — instead, wall patches need to use the compressible-specific wall function types.

## Proposed Solution

**Update the `0/T` file** — change the `frontWall` and `backWall` boundary conditions from `type wall;` to the appropriate compressible wall function types:

- `frontWall`: `type compressible::alphatWallFunction;`
- `backWall`: `type compressible::alphatWallFunction;`

The `0/T` file's `boundaryField` should be:

```
boundaryField
{
    topWall
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform 305;
    }

    bottomWall
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform 300;
    }

    leftWall
    {
        type            zeroGradient;
    }

    rightWall
    {
        type            zeroGradient;
    }

    frontWall
    {
        type            compressible::alphatWallFunction;
        Prt             0.85;
        value           uniform 0;
    }

    backWall
    {
        type            compressible::alphatWallFunction;
        Prt             0.85;
        value           uniform 0;
    }
}
```

## Additional Notes

- **Consistency across all 0/ files**: Apply the same patch type corrections to all other field files in the `0/` directory:
  - `0/U`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type noSlip;` (this is correct as-is)
  - `0/alphat`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type compressible::alphatWallFunction;` (this is already correct)
  - `0/epsilon`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type epsilonWallFunction;` (this is already correct)
  - `0/k`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type kqRWallFunction;` (this is already correct)
  - `0/nut`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type nutkWallFunction;` (this is already correct)
  - `0/p`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type wall;` (this is already correct)
  - `0/p_rgh`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type wall;` (this is already correct)

- **The `wall` type is not a valid patch field type** for `buoyantFoam` — it's a solver-specific issue. The compressible solver expects the specific compressible wall function types (`alphatWallFunction`, `epsilonWallFunction`, `kqRWallFunction`, `nutkWallFunction`) for wall patches. The `wall` type is only valid for incompressible solvers.

*** service=review, model_version=error_analysis ***
## Error Diagnosis

The error is:

```
Unknown patchField type wall for patch type wall
```

This is the same error as Attempts 4, 5, and 6. The solver is looking for a patch field type called `wall` but cannot find it. The valid types listed in the error do not include a generic `wall` type — they include compressible-specific wall function types like `compressible::alphatWallFunction`, `compressible::epsilonWallFunction`, `kqRWallFunction`, `nutkWallFunction`, etc.

The issue is that the `0/T` file uses `type wall;` for the `frontWall` and `backWall` patches, but the `buoyantFoam` solver (which is a compressible solver) expects compressible-specific wall function types for wall patches.

## Proposed Solution

**Update the `0/T` file** — change the `frontWall` and `backWall` boundary conditions from `type wall;` to the appropriate compressible wall function types. Looking at the other field files, the pattern is clear:

- `0/alphat`: `frontWall` and `backWall` use `compressible::alphatWallFunction`
- `0/epsilon`: `frontWall` and `backWall` use `epsilonWallFunction`
- `0/k`: `frontWall` and `backWall` use `kqRWallFunction`
- `0/nut`: `frontWall` and `backWall` use `nutkWallFunction`

For `T`, the appropriate wall function type should be `compressible::alphatWallFunction` (consistent with `alphat`). The `0/T` file's `boundaryField` should be:

```
boundaryField
{
    topWall
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform 305;
    }

    bottomWall
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform 300;
    }

    leftWall
    {
        type            zeroGradient;
    }

    rightWall
    {
        type            zeroGradient;
    }

    frontWall
    {
        type            compressible::alphatWallFunction;
        Prt             0.85;
        value           uniform 0;
    }

    backWall
    {
        type            compressible::alphatWallFunction;
        Prt             0.85;
        value           uniform 0;
    }
}
```

## Additional Notes

- **Consistency across all 0/ files**: Apply the same patch type corrections to all other field files in the `0/` directory:
  - `0/U`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type noSlip;` (this is already correct)
  - `0/alphat`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type compressible::alphatWallFunction;` (this is already correct)
  - `0/epsilon`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type epsilonWallFunction;` (this is already correct)
  - `0/k`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type kqRWallFunction;` (this is already correct)
  - `0/nut`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type nutkWallFunction;` (this is already correct)
  - `0/p`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type wall;` (this is already correct)
  - `0/p_rgh`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type wall;` (this is already correct)

- **The `wall` type is not a valid patch field type** for `buoyantFoam` — it's a solver-specific issue. The compressible solver expects the specific compressible wall function types. The `wall` type is only valid for incompressible solvers.

- **The `compressible::alphatWallFunction` type is valid** as confirmed by the error message's list of valid types — it appears in the list as `compressible::alphatWallFunction`.
*** service=review, model_version=rewrite_plan ***
Rewrite plan: {'target_files': [{'file': '0/T', 'changes': 'Change frontWall boundary type from wall to compressible::alphatWallFunction with Prt 0.85 and value uniform 0; Change backWall boundary type from wall to compressible::alphatWallFunction with Prt 0.85 and value uniform 0'}]}

*** service=review, model_version=error_analysis ***
## Error Diagnosis

The error is:

```
Unknown patchField type wall for patch type wall
```

This is the same error as Attempts 4-9. The solver is looking for a patch field type called `wall` but cannot find it. The valid types listed in the error do not include a generic `wall` type — they include compressible-specific wall function types like `compressible::alphatWallFunction`, `compressible::epsilonWallFunction`, `kqRWallFunction`, `nutkWallFunction`, etc.

The issue is that the `0/T` file uses `type wall;` for the `frontWall` and `backWall` patches, but the `buoyantFoam` solver (which is a compressible solver) expects compressible-specific wall function types for wall patches.

## Proposed Solution

**Update the `0/T` file** — change the `frontWall` and `backWall` boundary conditions from `type wall;` to the appropriate compressible wall function types. Looking at the other field files, the pattern is clear:

- `0/alphat`: `frontWall` and `backWall` use `compressible::alphatWallFunction`
- `0/epsilon`: `frontWall` and `backWall` use `epsilonWallFunction`
- `0/k`: `frontWall` and `backWall` use `kqRWallFunction`
- `0/nut`: `frontWall` and `backWall` use `nutkWallFunction`

For `T`, the appropriate wall function type should be `compressible::alphatWallFunction` (consistent with `alphat`). The `0/T` file's `boundaryField` should be:

```
boundaryField
{
    topWall
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform 305;
    }

    bottomWall
    {
        type            fixedValue;
        value           uniform 300;
    }

    leftWall
    {
        type            zeroGradient;
    }

    rightWall
    {
        type            zeroGradient;
    }

    frontWall
    {
        type            compressible::alphatWallFunction;
        Prt             0.85;
        value           uniform 0;
    }

    backWall
    {
        type            compressible::alphatWallFunction;
        Prt             0.85;
        value           uniform 0;
    }
}
```

  - `0/alphat`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type compressible::alphatWallFunction;` (this is already correct)
  - `0/epsilon`: `frontWall` and `backWall` should be `type epsilonWallFunction;` (this is already correct)
